  13. What do you do when your Norelco cutters become dull? You either buy new cutter and comb sets or a new expensive replacement head (RQ10). Now they make it difficult to change out the cutters on the latest models. The older Norelco shavers are very easy to pop in new cutters but this new 1 piece shaver head takes a little brain power to figure out. Here is how to disassemble this head unit and remove the cutters to be sharpened by hand. It's actually very easy! Do one cutter at a time. All you need is a very hard Arkansas sharpening stone. 1. Open up one blade cutter and use a miniature flat screwdriver to pop off the plastic ring surrounding the cutter. At the 9 & 3 o'clock position there are 2 tabs. simply pry up the black plastic ring at these 2 points and the ring will pop off. 2. The cutter-comb assembly will then be able to be removed. The stainless steel ring will remain connected to the head unit. Leave it this way. 3. Notice that the round metal comb assembly has 3 notches (2-small & 1-larger). Important when reassembling! 4. Using a stiff toothbrush, soak these items in hot soapy water and scrub them with the brush. Easy to get squeaky clean! 5. When finished, dry them-then on a hard Arkansas sharpening stone, put a drop of fine oil and in a circular motion sharpen the cutter. Takes just a few strokes! Don't press too hard. 6. Now reassemble the blade and comb. Turn the comb so the notches match up with the plastic assembly. Now insert the rotary blade cutter. Match up the plastic comb and cutter assembly so the 4 nodules fit inside the stainless steel ring. Now match the nodules of the black plastic locking ring, press down on it at the tabs and snap it into place. That's all there is to it! Now move on to the other 2 cutters. 7. When finished, your head unit will cut like new! NORELCO DOESN'T TELL YOU HOW TO DO THIS-THEY JUST WANT TO SELL YOU A NEW HEAD UNIT. Some vendors charge up to $60 for this replacement head (RQ10)!to $60 for this replacement head (RQ10)!

  780. After more than a decade of my faithfully using this razor, and no plans for using any other, I think I have a good handle on its attributes, so I'll just begin here...<br /><br />First of all, it's a very good shaver. It rarely pulls at the skin, or burns, or nicks. Yes, there might be those with one feature or other that can top it, but for a good all-around shaver -- which is really all that should count at the heart of it -- I'm very satisfied with this one.<br /><br />SHAVING QUALITY: It`s very good...I don't know if I'm embarrassed or proud when I admit this, but I've only changed the heads twice in my 11+ years, and that's a ridiculously low amount (they recommend yearly .) Part of it was frugality, but the major part of it has been the fact that I'm pleased with the razor as it is. I simply don't think it needs it. As I keep up a pretty good regimen of cleaning it almost every single time I shave, then I don't have any problems shaving. Simple.<br /><br />(Incidentally, I have never had any success shaving with a wet beard...I always make sure that my face is dry. While it may be able to be cleaned under the faucet, I have found that the act of shaving with a wet beard causes clumping of the hairs in the razor heads.)<br /><br />SHAVING COMFORT: It's good overall. I admit that it's not as smooth as, say, the best shave a quality hand razor can give when it's brand new. But it's always good, and when kept clean it shaves comfortably, close, and leaves my face feeling smooth, and fine...no burning sensations from over-shaving, nor ever having had the feeling that I have nicked myself.<br /><br />ONE IMPORTANT NOTE: As shaver manufacturers will tell you, don't switch to an electric shaver and expect a perfect shave right out of the box. I'll confirm what they tell you: you have to wait for several shaves with an electric for it to \\"find\\" that comfort zone. It's as much your skin as it is the electronic razor: they just need time to get acquainted before you can say whether you like the shaver.<br /><br />As for the Arcitec, you can see that the razors within the heads move in a circular motion within their housings. Each of the three razor heads move independently of the other, which I find really helpful when I'm switching from, say, my chin to my cheek. You don't want an unbending razor there, as you'll either miss whole areas or \\"burn\\" your skin. It's a nice system, and primarily why the shaves are so comfortable.<br /><br />COST: Here's where this can't be beaten by straight razors. You have a one-time cost of purchasing it. After that, it's almost cost free. And when you consider what it costs to buy a quality hand razor, and add to that the cost of replacing those blades on a regular basis for the life of that razor, and you know what I mean. There's almost no way to use a brand-name hand razor cheaply...those blades are ridiculously expensive. (And I am not swayed by the thought that two-, three-, four-, or even five-bladed razors are better than a single good razor.) And then there's shaving cream, and so on. This shaver is a one-time expense. That's it. (And need I mention the environmental waste of those plastic disposable razors?)<br /><br />MAINTENANCE: What could be simpler? Even if I admit that I'm probably woefully behind in my blade replacement, this is a product that has lasted quite well with little maintenance. And I'm still happy with my shave. Still, were I to replace the blades right now, the new heads on Amazon would cost me less than $50 which, I'll admit, isn't cheap, but I'll bet it's less than a six-month supply of fancy hand razor replacements.<br /><br />BATTERY INDICATOR: I don't think there's an electric razor out there that doesn't inform its user of a low battery, but this one simply does it in an extremely wise manner: it informs you of the minutes remaining EVERY TIME YOU PICK IT UP and use it. From its maximum charge in the 75-minute range until the single digits, you're aware of howmuch it has left. There's no having to guess whether you're getting low when you're heading away for the weekend: the remaining time is clearly displayed.<br /><br />THE TRIMMER: It's a great tool, and yes, you can get your hair caught in the other part while you're concentrating about your sideburns or elsewhere. The best prevention is to just detach the heads...the trimmer is an independent part, and it's just a two-second job each way of taking off the shaver heads and then replacing them when you're done. (The trimmer works really nicely, by the way.)<br /><br />All in all, I'm extremely pleased with the Philips Norelco Arcitec and can say truly, after over a decade, it's not going anywhere.when you're heading away for the weekend: the remaining time is clearly displayed.
